tobozo commented Aug 13, 2017

In an modified earlier release of esp8266_deauther I played with phonegap/cordova/cordovaduino to forward every HTTP message through the serial connection (deauther plugged to the android OTG) and also send orders to the ESP without using the web interface.

It wasn't working well, communications were slow and buggy, going further required some Java skills I don't have so I gave up.

But there is still a need to be able to communicate with the deauther while the WiFi connection is busy deauthing. While any client (App or browser) will be disconnected as soon as the deauthing starts, the deauther is still spamming logs through the serial and accepting orders.

Is it worth speculating on the stability of https://github.com/mik3y/usb-serial-for-android (I think Cordovaduino uses an old version of it) and asking for such a feature addition?

Great initiative anyway, very much appreciated!

tobozo changed the title from Serial Communication to [Feature request] Serial Communication Aug 13, 2017

tobozo referenced this issue in spacehuhn/esp8266_deauther Aug 13, 2017

tobozo Jun 6, 2018

The recommended settings for the serial:
https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wiki/spacehuhn/esp8266_deauther/img/howto_serial_2.jpg

Maybe lower the baud rate to 9600 in the deauther code and test its functionalities from a PC first, then try at 9600 on the Android?

Even at 9600 I had problems getting all the output forwarded to the android app though.

tobozo Jun 14, 2018

You tried random encodings but this setting is only for the output on the android side, feel free to choose UTF8 or your locale.

Instead of focusing on the deautheer, maybe get a proof of concept first using a simple local echo sketch :

void setup() {
  Serial.begin( 9600, SERIAL_8N1 );
}

void loop() {
  while(Serial.available()) {
    char c = Serial.read();
    Serial.print(c); // echo back
  }
}

Simplifying some terms of a problem can help separate concerns and pinpoint the origin of the issue.

There's a second argument at serial.begin(), see https://www.arduino.cc/en/serial/begin for an exhaustive list, maybe the library you're using requires 7N1 or 7N2?

What you could do is choose 8N1, 7N1 or another mode explicitely in your app, and compile the test sketch accordingly, then use the terminal to see if what you type is echoed back.
